</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Hydrogen vehicle</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydrogen_fuel_cell_vehicles&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen fuel cell vehicles">Hydrogen fuel cell vehicles</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg/300px-Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg/450px-Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg/600px-Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_FCV_reveal_25_June_2014_-_by_Bertel_Schmitt_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 2015 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Mirai" title="Toyota Mirai">Toyota Mirai</a> is one of the first hydrogen fuel cell vehicles to be sold commercially. The Mirai is based on the Toyota FCV concept car (shown).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <b>hydrogen vehicle</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicle</a> that uses <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> as its onboard fuel for <a href="/wiki/Motive_power" title="Motive power">motive power</a>. Hydrogen vehicles include hydrogen fueled <a href="/wiki/Space_rocket" class="mw-redirect" title="Space rocket">space rockets</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobiles</a> and other transportation vehicles. The power plants of such vehicles convert the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_energy" title="Chemical energy">chemical energy</a> of hydrogen to <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_energy" title="Mechanical energy">mechanical energy</a> either by burning hydrogen in an <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a>, or by reacting hydrogen with oxygen in a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a> to run electric motors. Widespread use of hydrogen for fueling transportation is a key element of a proposed <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_economy" title="Hydrogen economy">hydrogen economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hydrogen_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are 3 hydrogen cars publicly available in select markets; the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Mirai" title="Toyota Mirai">Toyota Mirai</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_ix35_FCEV" title="Hyundai ix35 FCEV">Hyundai ix35 FCEV</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Clarity" class="mw-redirect" title="Honda Clarity">Honda Clarity</a>. Several other companies are working to develop hydrogen cars. As of 2014, 95% of hydrogen is made from natural gas. It can be produced using renewable sources, but that is an expensive process.<sup id="cite_ref-Production_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Production-3">[3]</a></sup> Integrated wind-to-hydrogen (<a href="/wiki/Power_to_gas" title="Power to gas">power to gas</a>) plants, using <a href="/wiki/Electrolysis_of_water" title="Electrolysis of water">electrolysis of water</a>, are exploring technologies to deliver costs low enough, and quantities great enough, to compete with hydrogen production using natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The drawbacks of hydrogen use are high carbon emissions intensity when produced from natural gas, capital cost burden, low energy content per unit volume, production and compression of hydrogen, and the large investment in infrastructure that would be required to fuel vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-Berman2013_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berman2013-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cox2014_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox2014-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicles">Vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydrogen_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FCX_Clarity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/FCX_Clarity.jpg/220px-FCX_Clarity.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/FCX_Clarity.jpg/330px-FCX_Clarity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/FCX_Clarity.jpg/440px-FCX_Clarity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3209" data-file-height="1631" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FCX_Clarity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Honda <a href="/wiki/FCX_Clarity" class="mw-redirect" title="FCX Clarity">FCX Clarity</a>, a hydrogen fuel cell demonstration vehicle introduced in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_vehicle" title="Fuel cell vehicle">Fuel cell vehicle</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_bus" title="Fuel cell bus">Buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrail" title="Hydrail">trains</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHB_(bicycle)" title="PHB (bicycle)">PHB bicycles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal_boat_(hydrogen)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal boat (hydrogen)">canal boats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freight_bicycle_(hydrogen)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freight bicycle (hydrogen)">cargo bikes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf_cart" title="Golf cart">golf carts</a>, <a href="/wiki/ENV" title="ENV">motorcycles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_(hydrogen)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wheelchair (hydrogen)">wheelchairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_ship" title="Hydrogen ship">ships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airplane" title="Airplane">airplanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rockets</a> can already run on hydrogen, in various forms. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> used hydrogen to launch <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttles</a> into space. A working toy model car runs on <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, using a <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_fuel_cell" title="Regenerative fuel cell">regenerative fuel cell</a> to store energy in the form of hydrogen and <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> gas. It can then convert the fuel back into water to release the solar energy.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Since the advent of hydraulic fracturing the key concern for environmentalists with hydrogen fuel cell vehicles is consumer and public policy confusion that could result adoption of natural gas powered hydrogen vehicles with heavy hidden emissions to the detriment of environmentally friendly transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-Cox2014_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox2014-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current land speed record for a hydrogen-powered vehicle is 286.476 miles per hour (461.038&#160;km/h) set by <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Buckeye_Bullet" title="Buckeye Bullet">Buckeye Bullet 2</a>, which achieved a "flying-mile" speed of 280.007 miles per hour (450.628&#160;km/h) at the <a href="/wiki/Bonneville_Salt_Flats" title="Bonneville Salt Flats">Bonneville Salt Flats</a> in August 2008. For production-style vehicles, the current record for a hydrogen-powered vehicle is 207.297 miles per hour (333.612&#160;km/h) set by a prototype Ford Fusion Hydrogen 999 Fuel Cell Race Car at <a href="/wiki/Bonneville_Salt_Flats" title="Bonneville Salt Flats">Bonneville Salt Flats</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wendover" title="Wendover">Wendover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, in August 2007. It was accompanied by a large compressed oxygen tank to increase power.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobiles">Automobiles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydrogen_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Automobiles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">

</div>
</div>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN1474.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/DSCN1474.JPG/220px-DSCN1474.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/DSCN1474.JPG/330px-DSCN1474.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/DSCN1474.JPG/440px-DSCN1474.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
